  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a6ae1632-d982-443f-aae4-57fcf44a2607'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer13220922557914287581">Picoult brings to life a female prosecutor whose cherished family is shattered when she learns that her five-year-old son has been sexually abused.<br/><br/><i>What does it mean to be a good mother?<br/> How far would you go in the name of love -- and justice?</i><br/><br/>In the course of her everyday work, career-driven assistant district attorney Nina Frost prosecutes child molesters and works determi</span>
  <span id="freeText13220922557914287581" style="display:none">Picoult brings to life a female prosecutor whose cherished family is shattered when she learns that her five-year-old son has been sexually abused.<br /><br /><i>What does it mean to be a good mother?<br /> How far would you go in the name of love -- and justice?</i><br /><br />In the course of her everyday work, career-driven assistant district attorney Nina Frost prosecutes child molesters and works determinedly to ensure that a legal system with too many loopholes keeps these criminals behind bars. But when her own five-year-old son, Nathaniel, is traumatized by a sexual assault, Nina and her husband, Caleb, a quiet and methodical stone mason, are shattered, ripped apart by an enraging sense of helplessness in the face of a futile justice system that Nina knows all too well. In a heartbeat, Nina's absolute truths and convictions are turned upside down, and she hurtles toward a plan to exact her own justice for her son -- no matter the consequence, whatever the sacrifice.</span>

      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1934880119?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crumb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crumb" href="/user/show/53025065-crumb">Crumb</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12896668170700982083">Consider this:<br/><br/><b>What would you do in the name of justice? What would you do if someone harmed your child? And what would <i>you</i> do to protect them?</b><br/><br/>These are the questions Nina Frost was faced with after she found out that her son, Nathaniel, was sexually abused. Nina made a living as an assistant district attorney. Her job was to prosecute the child molestors and rapists that preyed on little girls and boys. In her subconscious, she reasoned with herself that through this line of work, her perfect wo</span>
  <span id="freeText12896668170700982083" style="display:none">Consider this:<br /><br /><b>What would you do in the name of justice? What would you do if someone harmed your child? And what would <i>you</i> do to protect them?</b><br /><br />These are the questions Nina Frost was faced with after she found out that her son, Nathaniel, was sexually abused. Nina made a living as an assistant district attorney. Her job was to prosecute the child molestors and rapists that preyed on little girls and boys. In her subconscious, she reasoned with herself that through this line of work, her perfect world could never be touched by the poison that she had locked away on a daily basis. <br /><br /><i>How could Nina be so wrong?</i><br /><br />When I pick up a book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7128.Jodi_Picoult" title="Jodi Picoult" rel="nofollow noopener">Jodi Picoult</a>, I know I am being placed in capable hands. She is an expert at the art of the written word. She is unafraid to approach controversial and sensitive topics and does so with grace and refinement. If I could use one word to describe this book.. it would simply be <b>exceptional</b>.</span>

<div id="review_54997420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54997420" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1363526-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217800966p2/1363526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54997420?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/1363526-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer54997420&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54997420" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer380597212238858352">I read this avidly – JP is a good writer – she draws characters well, pitches a story, and does her research. But there is a flaw in this book – Nina, commits murder in order to “protect” her sexually abused son from his abuser, and in doing so severely compounds the trauma suffered by him with the possibility that she may go to prison. Nina goes for the quick fix, the self-serving impassioned unthinking response – but, isn’t maternal instinct actually much stronger, much tougher, than that? I c</span>
  <span id="freeText380597212238858352" style="display:none">I read this avidly – JP is a good writer – she draws characters well, pitches a story, and does her research. But there is a flaw in this book – Nina, commits murder in order to “protect” her sexually abused son from his abuser, and in doing so severely compounds the trauma suffered by him with the possibility that she may go to prison. Nina goes for the quick fix, the self-serving impassioned unthinking response – but, isn’t maternal instinct actually much stronger, much tougher, than that? I can remember absolute terror engulfing me one night when faced with the realisation that my young children could be left motherless should anything happen to me. I remember willing myself to ... keep well...stay alive ...above all BE THERE....<br /><br />So, as I read, and admittedly read somewhat compulsively, Nina became more and more infuriating. She didn't behave like a mother behaves, she is arrogant, she is selfish, she is a know all, and by the end of the book I thoroughly disliked her – in fact come the court room summing up my sympathies lay squarely with the prosecution. At one point Nina reflects that in a “perfect world, love should be the only excuse one needs” ....uhhhh....no... loving is never an excuse for despicable appalling behaviour, loving is never "an excuse" for anything – and now I am getting as judgemental as Nina. <br /><br />That’s probably enough Jodie Picoult for while.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="380597212238858352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2287310088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2287310088" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4852457-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548981628p2/4852457.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287310088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9394002707213690446">Trigger: the sexual assault of a child. <br/><br/>This was a gut wrenching novel to read. Like many of Jodi Picoult’s novels you will have an internal debate on if justice through the court system is the best route. Though most of us would agree we should never take the law into our hand, we are also not blind to the injustices of our judicial system and corrections system. This powerful novel has twists and turns right up into the last couple pages. I was very engrossed in the plot. I did struggle with N</span>
  <span id="freeText9394002707213690446" style="display:none">Trigger: the sexual assault of a child. <br /><br />This was a gut wrenching novel to read. Like many of Jodi Picoult’s novels you will have an internal debate on if justice through the court system is the best route. Though most of us would agree we should never take the law into our hand, we are also not blind to the injustices of our judicial system and corrections system. This powerful novel has twists and turns right up into the last couple pages. I was very engrossed in the plot. I did struggle with Nina’s character; because I found her to be a bit obnoxious and arrogant (know it all for sure). However, as a group the characters were intriguing. <br /><br />My quick and simple overall: be prepared that this is an emotionally powerful novel. You’ll be entertained but you will have internal struggles of debate.</span>

  <span id="freeText17199100463292853162" style="display:none">I read this entire book in one night - no easy feat at over 400 pages, but it was so engrossing that I couldn't put it down. Picoult does such an incredible amount of research for every one of her books that, even if you don't like the story, you are guarenteed to come away with knowledge that could help you win "Who Wants to be a Millionaire". Reading too many Picoult books can get kind of annoying, as they all follow the same basic formula - even though the end is supposed to surprise you, after awhile, you know what to expect. Plus, the characters always get away with what they have done. Even though I become attached to the characters and don't want them to go to jail, in the back of my mind, I want one to get put away, just to mix things up!</span>

<div id="review_2167522480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2167522480" />
    <a title="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen"><img alt="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565231860p2/1256869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2167522480?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" href="/user/show/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen">Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=dumb">dumb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=fiction-lit">fiction-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=fpp-bad">fpp-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=word-vomit">word-vomit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=what">what</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=stupid-heroine">stupid-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2167522480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6543277936989892953">I firmly believe everyone should read what they want. What makes them happy. Be that shameless smut, or bad horror, or rapey bodice rippers. Read it all! I don't care!<br/><br/>But I, as a reader, have a guilty secret.<br/><br/>I'm a bit of a book snob.<br/><br/>This trait emerged without warning when I was recently discussing reading with a friend. She likes to read Jodi Picoult, as does her husband, and I have always sneered at Picoult books because they sound like Lifetime movies. We were trying to find books in common, s</span>
  <span id="freeText6543277936989892953" style="display:none">I firmly believe everyone should read what they want. What makes them happy. Be that shameless smut, or bad horror, or rapey bodice rippers. Read it all! I don't care!<br /><br />But I, as a reader, have a guilty secret.<br /><br />I'm a bit of a book snob.<br /><br />This trait emerged without warning when I was recently discussing reading with a friend. She likes to read Jodi Picoult, as does her husband, and I have always sneered at Picoult books because they sound like Lifetime movies. We were trying to find books in common, so she gave me three Picoult books to read, which I reluctantly took. (I, in turn, plan on giving her 90s teen romance, so I guess we'll be on equal ground after that.)<br /><br />So, I wasn't wrong about Picoult books. It was <i>exactly</i> like a Lifetime movie. Admittedly, I've only seen one, which was in high school, when I tried one afternoon to see what the big deal about Lifetime movies was. I freaking HATED it.<br /><br />And I hated this book.<br /><br />I've read legal thrillers before, and I've read books dealing with child molestation before. I've read books about motherhood before. Somehow Picoult manages to handle none of these topics well or with any originality. The legal aspect was stale, the molestation didn't move me to sympathy, and the motherhood parts dripped with excessive sentimentality, and I wanted to kill them with fire. Everything sucked. The characters sucked, especially Nina. She was a prosecutor who seemed to have only a casual understanding and respect for the law. She made no logical choices. She was one-dimensional. All the characters were one-dimensional.<br /><br />Everything was so BORING and STUPID. This book was a perfect example of why I never read Picoult. The writing was pretty basic, but with odd moments of attempted poetry. For example, how does someone chewing wintergreen mints give off green sparks? WTF? I also hated the religious aspect.<br /><br />And to top it all off, this was written in first person present tense. ARE YOU KIDDING ME.<br /><br />So now I have to return this book to my friend and figure out how to politely tell her what I thought. I still have the two other Picoult books she gave me, but I definitely need to cleanse my reading palate thoroughly before I pick them up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6543277936989892953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_79386072" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79386072" />
    <a title="Mandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2942631-mandy"><img alt="Mandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409477984p2/2942631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79386072?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy" href="/user/show/2942631-mandy">Mandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2942631-mandy?shelf=read-in-2006">read-in-2006</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer79386072&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79386072" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6936287636474813598">Precis: The story follows the reaction of a family to finding out their child has been abused.<br/><br/>I found this book quite disturbing, for all the wrong reasons. I mean for reasons probably not intended by the author.<br/><br/>First, the US judicial system and it's disadvantages for children victims of abuse, was detailed. It sounds medieval. Modern technology, used to help these children in Britain is not used at all in America. Children have to give evidence like adults. I found myself repelled by the method</span>
  <span id="freeText6936287636474813598" style="display:none">Precis: The story follows the reaction of a family to finding out their child has been abused.<br /><br />I found this book quite disturbing, for all the wrong reasons. I mean for reasons probably not intended by the author.<br /><br />First, the US judicial system and it's disadvantages for children victims of abuse, was detailed. It sounds medieval. Modern technology, used to help these children in Britain is not used at all in America. Children have to give evidence like adults. I found myself repelled by the method in America, and thankful that I am raising my children elsewhere.<br /><br />Then, the main character, is not at all nice. She is overbearing, rude, short tempered, lacking any patience, lives a double standard (she seems to encourage parents to put their children through the court system by omitting to inform them about the negative effects, when she knows full well she would not put her child through that same system). This unpleasant woman has a fabulous husband who adores her, though he is irritated by her, (which is okay) and a best friend/adorer who thinks she is a goddess, and can do no wrong. Quite simply he is totally unbelievable, and doesn't even seem that necessary to the story.<br /><br />The main character jumps to conclusions about who has abused her child and kills that person. She does this so fast, that she can have no regard for the sanctity of human life at all, and deserves to be flung into jail for the rest of her life. Her son does not deserve that, but he does not deserve such a minging mother anyway. I do not think the woman is a good mum. She isn't there much, she puts him into school when she supposes he is unwell (without trying to discover if he is or not) after dosing him up. In every description of her spending time with him, she is forcing him to do things that suit her needs, and have nothing to do with his, even when he has been abused, and is traumatised. She has a lot of memories of cute times with him, but they seem unreal. How can this monster of a mother have those recollections? Besides, they are the recollections of a stay at home mum, not a full on working mum.<br /><br />There was so little evidence that this guy was the one who had hurt her son that the fact that she killed him was truly amazing. If she had but waited, the DNA report would have come back. She didn't, although later in court, the fact that the DNA testing showed a match was held in her favour as proof that she had reasonably thought the abuser was the man she murdered. This woman is changed very little by having committed murder. She can trade witty comments the same, can give a great summing up the same, it made me want the world to be rid of her.<br /><br />Why kill him in court? She could easily have done it on the night she watched him through his lounge window, why do it in court?<br /><br />The conclusion, where it is revealed that her husband has murdered the true abuser is simply terrifying. It more or less says, if you live in America, and your child is abused, the only recourse you have to justice that will not harm your child is to kill the abuser. And if you get it wrong, you are not a bad person as you were trying to get it right. You should get away with it.<br /><br />I dread the future for that boy, living with two murderers (they are a perfect match after all), denied the chance to participate in justice for his abuser. Thank God he is not real. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6936287636474813598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2764911216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2764911216" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781416549369" href="/book/show/1521414.Perfect_Match">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=political">political</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=totally-overrated">totally-overrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=2019-booksread">2019-booksread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4911921-jen-from-quebec-0?shelf=tbt-soon">tbt-soon</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2764911216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15780077365000168833">Dang-- until the last 50 pages or so, this book was going to get a higher star rating. However, the ending was a bit too much of a 'picture perfect super happy' ending for my tastes; ESPECIALLY considering that the book deals with such negative topics! (sexual abuse, murder, rape, the flaws in the legal system, etc). <br/>I feel that the author took the easy way out + tried to tie things up into a pretty bow, and (by her own admission in the Author's Q+A section at the back of the book) actually went</span>
  <span id="freeText15780077365000168833" style="display:none">Dang-- until the last 50 pages or so, this book was going to get a higher star rating. However, the ending was a bit too much of a 'picture perfect super happy' ending for my tastes; ESPECIALLY considering that the book deals with such negative topics! (sexual abuse, murder, rape, the flaws in the legal system, etc). <br />I feel that the author took the easy way out + tried to tie things up into a pretty bow, and (by her own admission in the Author's Q+A section at the back of the book) actually went out of her way to RESEARCH LOOPHOLES in the state laws of her Maine setting in order for everything to end well. Ugh. Disappointing. For the majority of the book, Jodi Picoult was quite brave in her writing, not shying away from topics that are not tackled very often in contemporary 'chick lit'. For example, she shows how sexually abused children are often denied justice in the USA, as her District Attorney main character, Nina, had only 7 convictions for every 60 cases. Children with learning disabilities are hit hardest, as they are often unable to be 'found competent to stand witness at trial'. To have a book use 450 pages to show that the legal system is flawed for helpless victims only to throw away that good writing for 50 pages of tripe at the end really rather ruined the entire novel for me.<br />There are other thoughts that I have, as this is the 1st Jodi Picoult that I've read, but at the moment my emotions are hindering my writing! Bummer. --Jen from Quebec :0(</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340960530" href="/book/show/3104031-perfect-match">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=physical-books">physical-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186830167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4095958887878213952">Although this may not be one of Jodi Picoult's best novels, nevertheless it is still a good read. Most of Picoult's novel are about extraordinary situations that seem like they've come straight from newspaper headlines, and this one is no different – the sexual abuse of a five year old boy by a person they trusted. <br/><br/>Perfect Match is well-written, with multiple narrators so the reader feels like they get to observe all sides of the story. The characters are engaging, intricately flawed and realist</span>
  <span id="freeText4095958887878213952" style="display:none">Although this may not be one of Jodi Picoult's best novels, nevertheless it is still a good read. Most of Picoult's novel are about extraordinary situations that seem like they've come straight from newspaper headlines, and this one is no different – the sexual abuse of a five year old boy by a person they trusted. <br /><br />Perfect Match is well-written, with multiple narrators so the reader feels like they get to observe all sides of the story. The characters are engaging, intricately flawed and realistic. I don’t want to give any spoilers away but the author does raise some interesting questions in the novel regarding the issue of 'an eye for an eye' and just how far is too far to go when a parent is seeking protection and justice for their child. <br /><br />There were some things in this book that I didn't like. Again I don't want to give away any spoilers, but I didn't like the ending of the novel. I felt that the verdict of the trial should have gone the other way. <br /><br />Four stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4095958887878213952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127575867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer430835030574812230">I'm embarrassed by my not only enjoying Jodi Picoult in the beginning, but by how I seem to continue enjoying it even when she churns out stuff like this. Perfect Match is contradictory and angsty and ridiculous. Adultery, murder, child abuse... it is so crammed with controversial topics that it runs the whole gauntlet of shocking and comes back round to boring. Which is exactly what the book club readers like, no? A little of nitty gritty to discuss over the tea and biscuits, but not so much th</span>
  <span id="freeText430835030574812230" style="display:none">I'm embarrassed by my not only enjoying Jodi Picoult in the beginning, but by how I seem to continue enjoying it even when she churns out stuff like this. Perfect Match is contradictory and angsty and ridiculous. Adultery, murder, child abuse... it is so crammed with controversial topics that it runs the whole gauntlet of shocking and comes back round to boring. Which is exactly what the book club readers like, no? A little of nitty gritty to discuss over the tea and biscuits, but not so much that it's distasteful.<br /><br />Believe me, I'm not saying "Give me distasteful!" But I am saying "Stop giving me trite!" The books hinges on a coincidence that would barely ever ever happen in real life, but that's not what bothered me. (Fair play to Picoult for thinking of it.) What really riled me is this: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that the heroine (ha! heroine!) gets away with the murder - even though it is committed in front of a couple of hundred of people in a court of law. I mean, seriously? She gets away with it. Will any of Jodi Picoult's beloved and annoying creations ever be put behind bars? I bloody well hope so.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I gave this 2.5 stars but I know it won't put me off reading her others - if there are more to read. Blimey, have I read them all yet? I can't seem to help it: she is mindlessly addictive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="430835030574812230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3591675920708075056">I read all of Jodi Picoult's novels years ago and picked this one up a second time to take a break from my regular YA reading. It delighted and surprised me all over again. What a master storyteller! <br/><br/>The story takes off with a bang when Nina Frost, a prosecutor for sexual abuse cases, finds out that her own five-year-old son has been a victim of sexual abuse. There are several twists to determine who the real abuser is because her son has stopped talking as a result of his trauma. Mistakes are m</span>
  <span id="freeText3591675920708075056" style="display:none">I read all of Jodi Picoult's novels years ago and picked this one up a second time to take a break from my regular YA reading. It delighted and surprised me all over again. What a master storyteller! <br /><br />The story takes off with a bang when Nina Frost, a prosecutor for sexual abuse cases, finds out that her own five-year-old son has been a victim of sexual abuse. There are several twists to determine who the real abuser is because her son has stopped talking as a result of his trauma. Mistakes are made. People die. People go to trial. In the end the reader is left trying to sort out whether or not justice has really been served.<br /><br />Don't make people in Maine angry. They might get away with killing you. :-)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3591675920708075056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7723544986988085146">Where do I start with this atrocious book?<br/><br/>First of all, the main character Nina was a ridiculous c—t. Sorry, but it’s true. After finding out that her son is molested she decides to shoot the accused priest at the arraignment. How stupid is that? Even the angriest of parents wouldn’t do such a thing.   <span id="freeText7723544986988085146" style="display:none">Where do I start with this atrocious book?<br /><br />First of all, the main character Nina was a ridiculous c—t. Sorry, but it’s true. After finding out that her son is molested she decides to shoot the accused priest at the arraignment. How stupid is that? Even the angriest of parents wouldn’t do such a thing. If your child is molested your primary focus should be supporting and seeking help for your child. Not ending up in jail thereby reducing your son’s support system. <br /><br />And then… oopsie!! She killed the wrong guy! So now she is going on trial for murder. And then she decides to have an affair with the police officer (because Jodi always has to cram a contrived romantic subplot in every one of her novels). The author clearly has an agenda against the husband and wants us to feel like Nina’s affair is justified. Except she never gives us a good reason as to why we shouldn’t like her husband besides the fact that he is a little distant. <br /><br />Additionally, the 5 year old kid was completely unrealistic in the way that he talked. He used elaborate metaphors and SAT words that no five year old kid would ever use.<br /><br />The most ludicrous part of the book was the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She gets away with it because of the “love of her kid” or some BS like that. Ridiculous! No one in real life would get away with that. Why does the author completely ignore the fact that she SHOT AND KILLED AN INNOCENT MAN! What about HIS family and friends who are mourning their loved one that was wrongfully accused of molestation and then killed? Picoult was trying to make a moral dilemma out of something that was pretty straightforward.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And THEN the next stupid twist reveals that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the husband killed the REAL priest. Oh great! Now the kid has two murderous parents! Yipee! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This was the most ridiculous, pile of garbage I have ever had the misfortune of reading and I wouldn’t recommend this drivel to my worst enemy. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18370139790128139860">My all time favorite ofJodi Picoult's books. It took me a long time to open a JP book simply because the subject matter she chooses makes me squirmy. I felt the same way about this one. Most of us don't want to read a book about such an uncomfortable subject. The molestation is only a small part of the book, it is just the catalyst. The story grabs you within the first few chapters and refuses to let go. JP takes us a roller coaster of emotions and twists of events that continue until the end. O</span>
  <span id="freeText18370139790128139860" style="display:none">My all time favorite ofJodi Picoult's books. It took me a long time to open a JP book simply because the subject matter she chooses makes me squirmy. I felt the same way about this one. Most of us don't want to read a book about such an uncomfortable subject. The molestation is only a small part of the book, it is just the catalyst. The story grabs you within the first few chapters and refuses to let go. JP takes us a roller coaster of emotions and twists of events that continue until the end. One of the most surprising things about this book is the fact that I liked it so much while not liking the main character. I have heard this from friends of mine too. I have loaned it to several friends and they have loved it and I have always received the same comment "I couldn't put it down. It was just so good!" I have only loaned it to women so far so I can't give a man's perspective. You won't waste your money on this one. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2818745965364987413" style="display:none">If you've read one of Jodi Picoult's book then you've read "Perfect Match". My friend gave me this book and its been staring at me for the last three months. I decided to give the book a read and I don't know how I made it to the end.   <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249006168?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249006168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16936317828443441258">Jodi Picoult is one of my all time favorite authors. I anxiously await her new books each year.<br/><br/>It has been awhile since I read Perfect Match but it is a book that definitely stays with you. Painful to read at times but well written and difficult to put down once you start. You can tell that as usual Jodi Picoult has done her research. <br/><br/>As with quite a few of her books dealing with a tough subject can make for some emotional moments for sure. <br/><br/>Recommended <br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16048381687232595693">A gut-wrenching story. Like many of Jodi Picoult’s novels, you will ponder over whether justice through the court system is the best route or should one take matters into their own hands considering the gravity of the offense. Though most of us would agree we should let the law take its course, we are also aware of the loopholes and intricacies of the law and of our judicial system. <br/><br/>The story revolved around Nina, a defense attorney who handles legal cases involving child sexual abuse. Her world</span>
  <span id="freeText16048381687232595693" style="display:none">A gut-wrenching story. Like many of Jodi Picoult’s novels, you will ponder over whether justice through the court system is the best route or should one take matters into their own hands considering the gravity of the offense. Though most of us would agree we should let the law take its course, we are also aware of the loopholes and intricacies of the law and of our judicial system. <br /><br />The story revolved around Nina, a defense attorney who handles legal cases involving child sexual abuse. Her world is turned upside down when her own son is a victim of abuse and she has to fight for justice for her son. <br /><br />An emotional and heart-wrenching story.</span>

<div id="review_3013651910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3013651910" />
    <a title="Johara " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4184297-johara"><img alt="Johara " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605868397p2/4184297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3013651910?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johara " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johara " href="/user/show/4184297-johara">Johara </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444754582" href="/book/show/21260337-perfect-match">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3013651910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3657927298069903095">With Jodi Picoult…. You are never disappointed. She will always choose a controversial topic, and gets you connected with the characters, the twists and turns of the story, and the surprises that comes with it. She is a safe choice for me and have always enjoyed her writings.<br/><br/>And this time she chose a topic that’s more difficult as it’s something no parent ever wants to happen to their child. Assistant District Attorney finds out that her kid was raped, and instead of sticking to the system, she </span>
  <span id="freeText3657927298069903095" style="display:none">With Jodi Picoult…. You are never disappointed. She will always choose a controversial topic, and gets you connected with the characters, the twists and turns of the story, and the surprises that comes with it. She is a safe choice for me and have always enjoyed her writings.<br /><br />And this time she chose a topic that’s more difficult as it’s something no parent ever wants to happen to their child. Assistant District Attorney finds out that her kid was raped, and instead of sticking to the system, she takes matters in her hands. There is no spoiler here, as it was mentioned right at the begging of the story, so no surprise there. However, there are many surprises, and revelations throughout the story, raising more questions about the legal system, child abuse, the trauma they go through, and the lack of support. Plus, what would you do as a parent if you were in her place. The story gives you each characters’ perspective, and how things turn for each one of them. <br /><br />Some parts were quite hard to read, which the author herself admitted that she had a difficult time to write, being a parent herself. Despite all that, I won’t say that this is the best work of Jodi Picoult that I’ve read so far, as there were far better stories for her, and I was leaning toward giving this book a 3 stars, but the last few pages had the unexpected turn of events, which is no surprise with Picoult as she seems to like doing that a lot, so I gave this book 4 stars. Okay I admit, I like her. That's why :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3657927298069903095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96966095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96966095" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3534502-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462743596p2/3534502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96966095?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/3534502-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96966095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5163391256798310794">What a story! Picoult is my favorite author and all of her books seem to deal with some sort of moral or social dilemma. This was a superb drama. One that tugs at the heart of every parent out there. Who hasn't imagined being a vigilante of justice in the event that your child was victimized?<br/><br/>The book was written in first person from many of the characters points of view. At first, when I was just getting to know and understand the characters, this was a little difficult to follow. I quickly over</span>
  <span id="freeText5163391256798310794" style="display:none">What a story! Picoult is my favorite author and all of her books seem to deal with some sort of moral or social dilemma. This was a superb drama. One that tugs at the heart of every parent out there. Who hasn't imagined being a vigilante of justice in the event that your child was victimized?<br /><br />The book was written in first person from many of the characters points of view. At first, when I was just getting to know and understand the characters, this was a little difficult to follow. I quickly overcame that problem and was sucked into the heart of this story. The characters were written with such depth; they really came to life for me as a reader. I both cried with them and rejoiced with them while I was reading. There was a huge plot twist about 2/3 of the way through the story that actually made me gasp out loud! And the ending, while a little short on explanation, left me very satisfied with the outcome of everyone.<br /><br />I read some of the other reviews out there on Goodreads and I was surprised to see that some people mentioned reading this book in one sitting. It was too intense of a read for me to be able to do that.<br /><br />Another excellent book by Jodi Picoult. This is why she is my favoite author.....</span>
  <a data-text-id="5163391256798310794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1263326464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263326464" />
    <a title="Marti Dahlquist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23974616-marti-dahlquist"><img alt="Marti Dahlquist" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263326464?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marti Dahlquist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marti Dahlquist" href="/user/show/23974616-marti-dahlquist">Marti Dahlquist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1263326464&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263326464" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3912318231027826271">There was too much self justification in all of the characters for me to like this book. The main character barely missed a beat when it turns out she murdered the wrong person. She convinces her son that people who molest young boys are "bad" but it fails to register in her head that people who murder are also bad.<br/><br/>I'd like to know that all professionals take their job seriously and treat each case as if it happened to a family member. The fact that her son was too special to endure what she had</span>
  <span id="freeText3912318231027826271" style="display:none">There was too much self justification in all of the characters for me to like this book. The main character barely missed a beat when it turns out she murdered the wrong person. She convinces her son that people who molest young boys are "bad" but it fails to register in her head that people who murder are also bad.<br /><br />I'd like to know that all professionals take their job seriously and treat each case as if it happened to a family member. The fact that her son was too special to endure what she had put other children through was obnoxious. The fact that every person involved with her trial bent over backwards to get her off was unsettling. It didn't make me want to ever have to rely on the legal system because apparently it is only on your side when you work for it. I realize this is fiction, but the story was just too terrible to enjoy.<br /><br />It was also quite obvious that the husband had something to do with the murder of the real molester. The fact that both he and the cat turned up dead at the same time led you to believe someone in the story did it.<br /><br />I normally enjoy Jodi Picoult, but not this one.....</span>
  <a data-text-id="3912318231027826271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s+qm39/UTa4ul04mlYtSOiqpU2khIvP+hvdN8a1PPbwaoKrA/T97F15l5QaZ9pKYQPGm1kJ8LbUUhbGPcoSS4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  <span id="freeText18412354673361296307" style="display:none">Jodi Picoult is the author of twenty-six novels, including the #1 New York Times bestsellers Small Great Things, A Spark of Light, Leaving Time, The Storyteller, Lone Wolf, Between the Lines, Sing You Home, House Rules, Handle with Care, Change of Heart, Nineteen Minutes, and My Sister’s Keeper. She lives in New Hampshire with her husband and three children.<br /><br />Her new novel, THE BOOK OF TWO WAYS, is available in hardcover, ebook, and audio on September 22nd.<br /><br />Website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jodipicoult.com/">http://www.jodipicoult.com/</a><br /><br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/jodipicoult">https://www.facebook.com/jodipicoult</a> <br /><br />Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/jodipicoult">https://twitter.com/jodipicoult</a><br /></span>
